## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: This task involves modeling the rate of change of concentration (dA/dt) as a function of time and concentration in a chemical reaction. This is a classic chemical kinetics problem where the rate law relates the reaction rate to the concentration of reactants, possibly with time-dependent effects.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- {'name': 'Zero-order kinetics', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0', 'scenario': 'Reaction rate independent of concentration'}
- {'name': 'First-order kinetics', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A', 'scenario': 'Rate proportional to concentration (radioactive decay, unimolecular decomposition)'}
- {'name': 'Second-order kinetics', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A**2', 'scenario': 'Rate proportional to square of concentration (bimolecular reaction)'}
- {'name': 'nth-order kinetics', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A**c1', 'scenario': 'General power-law rate dependence on concentration'}
- {'name': 'Mixed-order kinetics (first + second)', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2', 'scenario': 'Competing first and second order reaction pathways'}
- {'name': 'Reversible first-order reaction', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A + c1', 'scenario': 'First-order forward reaction with constant reverse contribution (equilibrium approach)'}
- {'name': 'Saturation kinetics (non-Michaelis form)', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A**2 / (A + c1)', 'scenario': 'Second-order reaction with saturation at high concentration'}
- {'name': 'Autocatalytic reaction', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A)', 'scenario': 'Logistic-type autocatalytic kinetics where product catalyzes reaction'}
- {'name': 'Inhibited reaction kinetics', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A / (1 + c1 * A)**2', 'scenario': 'Substrate inhibition or product inhibition effects'}
- {'name': 'Time-dependent rate (radiation-driven)', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t)', 'scenario': 'Reaction with time-varying external driving (e.g., photolysis with varying intensity)'}
- {'name': 'Consecutive reaction intermediate', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * exp(c1 * t) + c2 * exp(c3 * t)', 'scenario': 'Concentration rate of an intermediate in consecutive reactions'}
- {'name': 'Third-order kinetics', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A**3', 'scenario': 'Termolecular reaction or effective third-order process'}
- {'name': 'Half-integer order kinetics', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A**0.5', 'scenario': 'Chain reaction mechanisms often yield fractional orders'}

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Negative rate of change with positive concentration → consumption kinetics: dA_dt = -c * A**n with c > 0
- Rate proportional to concentration raised to a non-integer power → chain reaction or complex mechanism with radical intermediates
- Rate that levels off at high concentration → saturation or inhibition, use rational functions A/(1+c*A)
- Rate that passes through zero and changes sign → reversible reaction approaching equilibrium, look for (A - A_eq) terms
- Quadratic dependence on A with a maximum → autocatalytic behavior, A*(c - A) structure
- Rate independent of time t → autonomous ODE, classical rate law dA/dt = f(A) only
- Explicit time dependence in rate → non-autonomous system, external forcing or sequential mechanism
- Concentration appearing in both numerator and denominator → enzyme-like or surface-catalyzed mechanism
